41 (232)
Various Gods
Gr╠еtsamada
21 verses: g─Бyatr─л, except anuс╣гс╣нubh 16тАУ17, and br╠еhat─л 18, arranged in trcas ╠е
This is a composite hymn: its composite nature is clear from its position in the maс╣Зс╕Нala, for with twenty-one verses it is far longer than the preceding hymn, which contains six. The hymn has been assembled from the three-verse units known as tr╠еcas. It is also of mixed meter, though g─Бyatr─л prevails for most of the hymn (vss. 1тАУ15 and 19тАУ21).
Nonetheless, with the exception of the final three verses (19тАУ21), the hymn forms a ritual unity, treating in order the gods addressed in a structured recitation form ing part of the Morning Pressing, which is found also in later Vedic ┼Ыrauta ritual, known as the Pra├╝ga┼Ыastra. Other instantiations of this recitation in the с╣Ъgveda are found in I.2тАУ3 (see remarks there) and I.23. The order of divinities is V─Бyu (1тАУ2), Indra-V─Бyu (3), Mitra-Varuс╣Зa (4тАУ6), A┼Ыvins (7тАУ9), Indra (10тАУ12), the All Gods (13тАУ 15), Sarasvat─л (16тАУ18). The last three verses (19тАУ21) are, according to Oldenberg (1888: 197 and n. 4), an independent tr╠еca, relating to the carts holding the oblation (havirdh─Бna carts), that was mistakenly incorporated into the hymn. Even if this last tr╠еca was a late addition, it is worth noting that the first and last verses of the hymn end with the word so╠Бmap─лtaye тАЬfor soma-drinking,тАЭ forming at least a nominal ring.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This tс╣Ыca is characterized by lexical chaining. The first p─Бda of vs. 2 reprises niy├║tv─Бn from 1c, v─Бyo from (accented) v─Б╠Бyo (1a), and ─Б╠Бgahi (1b). Vs. 3 is less closely tied to what precedes, but ┼Ыukr├б- тАШclearтАЩ, which characterizes the first drink of soma, offered to V─Бyu, is repeated in 3a from 2b, and niy├║tvant- also recurs from 1c and 2a. The impv. p├нbatam (3c) picks up (s├│ma-)p─лtaye from 1c. More subtly, ─Б╠Бy─Бtam repeats the preverb of ─Б╠Бgahi (1b, 2a) and also echoes the unrelated verb ay─Бmi of 2b.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This tс╣Ыca is characterized by lexical chaining. The first p─Бda of vs. 2 reprises niy├║tv─Бn from 1c, v─Бyo from (accented) v─Б╠Бyo (1a), and ─Б╠Бgahi (1b). Vs. 3 is less closely tied to what precedes, but ┼Ыukr├б- тАШclearтАЩ, which characterizes the first drink of soma, offered to V─Бyu, is repeated in 3a from 2b, and niy├║tvant- also recurs from 1c and 2a. The impv. p├нbatam (3c) picks up (s├│ma-)p─лtaye from 1c. More subtly, ─Б╠Бy─Бtam repeats the preverb of ─Б╠Бgahi (1b, 2a) and also echoes the unrelated verb ay─Бmi of 2b.

Griffith

Drawn by thy team, O Vayu, come; to thee is offered this, the pure.
Thou visitest the presser’s house.

Geldner

Mit dem Niyutgespann fahrend komm, o Vayu! Dieser klare Soma ist dir gereicht. Du pflegst in das Haus des Somabereiters zu kommen.

Grassmann

Mit Vielgespann, o V─Бju, komm, hier ward dir reiner Trank gereicht, Bald kommst du in des Pressers Haus.

English translation:

тАЬLeaders (of rites), Indra and V─Бyu, lords of the Niyut steeds, come and drink today the mixture of milk and of the pure Soma.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Of the clear (soma) today and of the one mixed with milk, with its teams, o Indra and V─БyuтАФ
drive here and drink it, men!

Jamison Brereton Notes

The stem niy├║tvant- (3b) is repeated from 1c and 2a, as noted above, but here as an apparent gen. sg. modifying the soma drink (or rather one of them), not a god or gods. Geldner (n. 3b) suggests that it is a metrically conditioned тАЬhypallageтАЭ for dual niy├║tvant─Б, which would qualify Indra and V─Бyu. This is a clever idea and would restore parallelism to the phraseology of the tс╣Ыca, though IтАЩm not sure thatтАЩs necessary: Rigvedic poets enjoy tweaking parallelism in the syntactic equivalent of a slant rhyme. Oldenberg floats a truly oddball idea, unworthy of his usual acuity: that niy├║tvant- should modify an unexpressed r├бthena but in the absence of a head noun in the proper case it gets sucked [not OldenbergтАЩs term] into the gen. by the тАЬbenachbarteтАЭ gen. Even if this were a reasonable explanation in principle – that an untethered adj.

could be captured by an adjacent or nearby word in another case – niy├║tvataс╕е is actually in a different p─Бda from the other genitives and is adjacent only to the dual dvandva ├нndr─Бv─Бy┼л.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This tс╣Ыca is characterized by lexical chaining. The first p─Бda of vs. 2 reprises niy├║tv─Бn from 1c, v─Бyo from (accented) v─Б╠Бyo (1a), and ─Б╠Бgahi (1b). Vs. 3 is less closely tied to what precedes, but ┼Ыukr├б- тАШclearтАЩ, which characterizes the first drink of soma, offered to V─Бyu, is repeated in 3a from 2b, and niy├║tvant- also recurs from 1c and 2a. The impv. p├нbatam (3c) picks up (s├│ma-)p─лtaye from 1c. More subtly, ─Б╠Бy─Бtam repeats the preverb of ─Б╠Бgahi (1b, 2a) and also echoes the unrelated verb ay─Бmi of 2b.

English translation:

тАЬShowerers of wealth, (bring to us) such (riches) that the malevolent man, or foe, whether he be far off or nigh, may not take (it) away.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Whether he be far of for nigh: na yat para n─Бntara: para = d┼лrastha, being at a distance;

Antara = sam─лpavart─л, on ebeing near; another interpretation: para = asambaddha, unconnected and antara = sambaddha, connected or related; Indra is the object: ‘Indra whom may such a man not overcome – yam indram na parabh┼лyat’

Jamison Brereton

So that no distant mortal nor one close by will dare against (you), you of bullish goodsтАФ
(and no) defaming cheat.

Griffith

Such, wealthy Gods! as none afar nor standing nigh to us may harm,
Yea, no malicious mortal foe.

Der kein Fremder noch Nahestehender Trotz bieten kann, kein ├╝belredender, feindseliger Sterblicher, ihr Schatzreiche!

Dass ferne nicht noch nahe uns, ein b├╢ser, falscher Sterblicher, O starke, zu bek├дmpfen wagt.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIf Indra provide for our happiness, evil will not come behidn us, good will be before us.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

And if Indra will have mercy on us, no evil will reach us from behind. There will be good for us in front.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The ca here is a subordinator (тАШifтАЩ) and conditions accent on mс╣Ыс╕╖├бy─Бti. See II.42.1.

There are several nice phonetic sequences: ab: тАж no, n├б naс╕е, where the 1st and last words are the same, with na┼Ыat at the end. And c: bhadr├бm bhav─Бti.

Griffith

Indra be gracious unto us: sin shall not reach us afterward,
And good shall be before us still.

Geldner

Wenn sich Indra unser erbarmen sollte, dann erreicht uns von hinten kein ├Ьbel, von vorn wird uns Gl├╝ck zuteil.

Grassmann

Wenn Indra uns gewogen ist, trifft nimmer Noth im R├╝cken uns, Und vor uns ist des Gl├╝ckes Glanz.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬLet Indra, the beholder of all, the conqueror of foes, send us security from all quarters.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Indra will make (us) without fear from all the regions round about. He is the one who conquers rivalsтАФthe boundless one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I am tempted to take j├йt─Б as a periphr. future, parallel as it is to the subjunctive karat. But this is not nec.

Griffith

From all the regions of the world let Indra send security,
The foe-subduer, swift to act.

English translation:

тАЬSarasvat─л, best of mothers, best of rivers, best of goddesses, we are, as it were, of no repute; grant us, mother, distinction.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ambitame, nad─лtame, devitame: the superlatives of ambik─Б, a mother, nad─л, a river and dev─л, a goddess

Jamison Brereton

O best mother, best river, best goddess, Sarasvat─лтАФ
we are like ones unlauded: make a laud for us, mother.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Like 15ab, the first two p─Бdas of this vs. consist entirely of accented vocatives.

Griffith

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the two, (Heaven and Earth), who confer good fortune upon the sacrifice, proceed (to the altar); for verily, we implore you both (to com), as well as Agni the bearer of oblations.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

May the two: The objects addressed are the two ┼Ыakaс╣нas, carts or barrows, which are employed to bring the fuel, or the Soma and are plural ced in front of the hall of sacrifice, north and south of an altar erected outside, and which are considered here as types of Heaven and Earth, who, properly speaking, are the deities of the Tс╣Ыca; the ┼Ыakaс╣нas are requested, according to S─Бyaс╣Зa, to proceed to the west part of the northern ved─л, or altar– uttaravedeс╕е pa┼Ыcimabh─Бgam pr─Бgacchat─Бm; according to K─Бty─Бyana, these are also termed havirdh─Бnas, oblation-containers, and part of the ceremony consists in dragging them into different positions at different periods, accompanied by appropriate texts, which are given in the Yajurveda 5.14-21

English translation:

тАЬMay the adorable gods, devoice of malice, sit down today nigh to you both to drink the Soma.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let the gods, deserving the sacrifice, sit in the lap of you two who are without deceit,
here today for the soma-drinking.

Griffith

In both your laps, ye guileless Ones, the Holy Gods shall sit them down
To-day to drink the Soma here.

Geldner

In euer beider Scho├Я, ihr Truglosen, sollen die opferw├╝rdigen G├╢tter heute hier zum Somatrunke sich setzen!

Grassmann

In euren Schooss, o freundliche, lasst heut die G├╢tter setzen sich, Die heiligen zum Somatrunk.

Elizarenkova

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЖ) (рд╡рд╛рдореН) рдпреБрд╡рдпреЛрдГ (рдЙрдкрд╕реНрдердореН) рдЙрдкрддрд┐рд╖реНрдардиреНрддрд┐ рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдБрд╕реНрддрдореН (рдЕрджреНрд░реБрд╣рд╛) рджреНрд░реЛрд╣рд╛рджрд┐рджреЛрд╖рд░рд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдГред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╕реБрдкрд╛рдорд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рдХрд╛рд░рд╛рджреЗрд╢рдГред (рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕рдГ (рд╕реАрджрдиреНрддреБ) (рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд┐рдпрд╛рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡реГрджреНрдзрд┐рдордпрдпрдЬреНрдЮрдкреНрд░рдЪрд╛рд░рд╛рд░реНрд╣рд╛рдГ (рдЗрд╣) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░реЗ (рдЕрджреНрдп) рдЗрджрд╛рдиреАрдореН (рд╕реЛрдордкреАрддрдпреЗ) рдпрдпрд╛ рд╕реЛрдорд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛рдгрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдпрдиреНрддреЗ рддрд╕реНрдпреИ реереирезрее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХ рд╡ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХ рдпрд╛рдВрдЪреНрдпрд╛рдЬрд╡рд│ рдирд┐рд░реНрджреЛрд╖ рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖реА рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛ рдЕрд╕рд╛рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдд. рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдореБрд│реЗ рд╕реНрддреНрд░реА-рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рдВрдордзреНрдпреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рд╡ рдЙрддреНрддрдо рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдг рд╕рдорд╛рди рдЕрд╕рд╛рд╡реЗ. рее реирез рее
